Kuṭāra Mānava L.Or. 2215

edited by Timothy Lubin, Eko Bastiawan & Marine Schoettel

Filename: DHARMA_DiplEdKutaraManavaLeidenOr2215.xml

Language: Old Javanese

Repository: Nusantara Philology (tfd-nusantara-philology)

Version: part commented since without access_token with github actions api calls are limited – still working on it

Witness

  • [Le1 ] Leiden, Leiden University Libraries (UB), Or. 2215
    • Hand Description: The manuscript has been written by more than one scribe. The first scribe appears to have two ways of writing ḍ. The less common type occurs twice in 6v1. Taling is sometimes canceled with hulu, as in 4v2, 6r2, 6r4. Sometimes the first of two talings in sequence is canceled; it would be more convenient to be able to encode that with ⟦⌈⟧ but we have rather deleted (See instances marked with below). There are a few instances of pasangan -ya being used instead of paten, especially after akṣara ra (e.g., 16v1, 2); could this be influenced by the similarlity of Javanese paten and Balinese pasangan -ya? The layar sometimes slants downward, sometimes upward. New scribal hands appear to begin on folio 33r, 48v, 54r and 61v (with this one, u and ū not distinguished at all). We have hyphenated reduplications, Javanese pair-compounds, and mixed compounds such as kalāntara-putra. Layar is often (but not always) written so as to overlap the contiguous aksaras; in many instances, it is clearly written over the first, but at the very beginning of 43v3 it is attached to the second aksara in the Indian fashion. Folio numeration is extremely faulty: often missing, wrong, corrected, or wrongly corrected (f. 60). On ff. 12-16, the scribe has written 22, 33, 44, 55, 77 (sic) by mistake. Some folios at the beginning and end are unnumbered.

Edition

. <handDesc>
55 <p>The manuscript has been written by more than one scribe.
. The first scribe appears to have two ways of writing ḍ. The less common type occurs twice in 6v1.
. Taling is sometimes canceled with hulu, as in 4v2, 6r2, 6r4.
. Sometimes the first of two talings in sequence is canceled; it would be more convenient to be able to encode that with <del>⌈</del> but we have rather deleted <seg>e</seg> (See instances marked with <!--@@ the first of two talings was deleted--> below).
. There are a few instances of pasangan -ya being used instead of paten, especially after akṣara ra (e.g., 16v1, 2); could this be influenced by the similarlity of Javanese paten and Balinese pasangan -ya?
60 The layar sometimes slants downward, sometimes upward.
. New scribal hands appear to begin on folio 33r, 48v, 54r and 61v (with this one, u and ū not distinguished at all).
. We have hyphenated reduplications, Javanese pair-compounds, and mixed compounds such as kalāntara-putra.
. Layar is often (but not always) written so as to overlap the contiguous aksaras; in many instances, it is clearly written over the first, but at the very beginning of 43v3 it is attached to the second aksara in the Indian fashion.
. Folio numeration is extremely faulty: often missing, wrong, corrected, or wrongly corrected (f. 60). On ff. 12-16, the scribe has written 22, 33, 44, 55, 77 (sic) by mistake. Some folios at the beginning and end are unnumbered.
65 </p>
. </handDesc>
. </physDesc>

samitra lavan duṣṭa, sapadulūra ⟦la⟧ ⟨⟨n la⟩⟩ van duṣṭa, Mmaroṅ lakṣa ri duṣṭa satuṅgal-tuṅgal
nora vnaṅ doṣanana pati denira saṅ amava bhumi; amateni voṅ tan padoṣa, akon amatenana voṅ tan padoṣa, anatoni voṅ tan padoṣa; duṣṭa tətlu iku, yan sayəkti sacihna, katlu ḍəṇḍa pati, arane katlu duṣṭa atoh avake, yan amalaku huripən iṅ saṅ amava bhumi, katlu ḍəṇḍanən pataṅ lakṣa vivijinən iṅ duṣṭa satuṅgalsatuṅgal kahilaṅane doṣane; hana dene kaṅ sapaṅan lāvan duṣṭa, sadulur lavan duṣṭa, amitra lāvan duṣṭa, aveh gnah riṅ duṣṭa, iku kalima paḍa ḍəṇḍanən aṅroṅ lakṣa J
